<Text>For my upcoming PCS move, Republic Moving and Storage was contracted to move my household goods.  While I don't have much of a choice when it comes to moving companies, I would choose Republic Moving and Storage again if I had the choice.

The communication prior to my move was excellent.  I received phone calls with week before, two days before, the day before, and the morning of, confirming my date and time for the move.  As anyone who has gone through a PCS move, timely communication is key and well appreciated.

<user_id>111570591109303807757<//user_id><name>Andy Stumpf<//name><time>1500046558036<//time><rating>1<//rating><Review>DO NOT use this company

Everything with our move started off well.  I had a professional and timely meeting with Skip, our estimator.   He handed me over to Amber, our move representative.  The process was straightforward, and this was the company (Republic) that had moved me multiple times while I served in the military without issue.  The packers showed up on time, and seemed quite professional.  Packing and loading went as expected.  We needed to have our household goods stored for less than one week at their facility which is no more than a few miles from our house.  We were charged 3k for these few days, and what we were apparently paying for during that time is for people to steal from us.

Our shipment arrived yesterday, with the first comment from the driver that he was surprised to find the truck unlocked (it arrived with no locks on it) when he attached his truck to it.  Things went downhill from there.

Each box is supposed to be labelled, both with its contents, and with a sticker so you can inventory items as they come off of the truck.  Nearly half of the boxes and items that came off of the truck had no sticker, and one word descriptions of the contents.  The inventory system that I was supposed to use as the customer was rendered completely useless by the lack of inventory stickers.  Multiple times throughout the day the unloading crew, which is local to our new home location, and deals with unloading moves on a daily basis commented that "they had never seen anything like this."  The crew asked us to come and photo document the loading condition of the vehicle because they did not want to be held liable for the contents.  Apparently they had a contest to see how fast they could pack our things, regardless of the damage it caused.  Multiple items were damaged, and we have barely begun to open the boxes.

We had declared high value items, none of which were given an inventory number, making them impossible to verify.  2 Imac desktop computers containing critical work material were packed (I watched them being packed) have mysteriously gone missing from the time they were packed at our house, until the time our shipment arrived at our new home.  The only stop along the way, the "warehouse" where our goods were supposedly stored.

The lack of inventory stickers, and the missing items were so obscene to the crew that unpacked us, that the driver did not feel comfortable signing the paperwork, and he escalated the situation to his boss, in an attempt to ensure his crew was not held liable.  Again, "I have never seen anything like this in 15 years" was a common theme.

I called and emailed Amber about an hour into the offload and expressed my concern for the condition of our goods (at this point I knew nothing of the missing items).  What you will get when you contact this company is quite simple:  Sorry, contact the claims department...Which is not directly associated with the movers.  Basically, take your complaint somewhere else, we already have your money.

I emailed both Skip and Amber later in the day expressing my concern, with a request they respond and confirm receipt of my email.  No response, which perfectly articulates how much this company cares.

I have yet to be able to contact the claims department, but I will begin that journey in a few hours.

There are plenty of reputable moving companies out there, please save yourself the pain and frustration by finding ANY other company than this one.

They don't care, period.< /Review>< Pics>

<name>Dex< /name><time>1620079958086<//time>< Rating>
4< /Rating>
< review>
There are a lot of trails you can enjoy. Great place for hiking, running, mountain biking and horseback riding. Some parts of the trails are steep, like the first half of Joice trail starting at Benal ranch, again Joice trail coming up from the east to Vista loop trail, Boundary trail near the Coyote Peak and the first half of Mine trail at Nored ranch . If you want thrill of MTB'ing, try the rocky ridge trail. Most of the trails have no shade, so you need sunscreen and lots of water. Sometimes you can see snakes, wild turkeys, dears along the trail. A couple of months ago, I spotted a group of wild boars.< /review>

This is a great safe place to go hiking. If you have a dog you are able to bring them as long as they are on a leash. Luckily every Trail is easy to find and even easier to find your way back. The bathrooms are super clean and they are always stocked with paper towels, toilet paper, and hand soap. Last time I went the meter to charge for parking was down but keep in mind that you should have cash on you just in case the ticket meter is working again. Last time I checked used to be $6.<//Text>

< userid>
104042685529602206608< /userid>
< username>
Marco Paganini</username>
< date>
1461389869308<//date>
<rate>5<//rate>< text>
Santa Teresa is my favorite park in San Jose. The park occupies a sizable area and has a fair amount of trails for hikers, bikers, and horse riders. The highest point in the park (Coyote Peak) offers a nice view of San Jose (but be prepared for the steep climb, especially if you're biking there.)

Santa Teresa is usually not very crowded, even on weekends. Weekdays are especially nice for those who enjoy activities like animal and bird watching, or a lone bike ride.

Unlike many other parks, leashed dogs *are* allowed here (but please, make sure your dog is on a leash!).The park also offers (clean) public restrooms and a large covered area which can be reserved for parties.

For mountain bikers, the park offers a wide range of biking trails, ranging from almost flat and easy to rocky and technical. No matter how experienced you are, you can always create a route that will get you entertained (and tired).

The only thing I miss in this park is a large body of water. There are a few seasonal streams running through the park, but no lakes.

The parking lot is fairly large, and parking was $6 last time I checked. Rangers do check the place and will give you tickets if you don't pay the parking fees or park your car on the road.<//text>

This is one of my favorite parks.  We hike, walk our dog, and mountain bike here regularly.  It's a great place for exercise, and you can easily get 2000 feet of mountain bike climbing in 8 miles of riding, with hills left over in case you have anything left over!  After rains the trails are muddy with soft clay and unsuitable for mountain biking (and sometimes a pain for hiking), and I wish they posted trail closures online.  The views are fantastic.<//text>

<Review>(Translated by Google) Come to Santa Teresa County Park, located ten miles south of downtown San Jose in the Santa Teresa Mountains. This 1,673-acre park has a rich history and spectacular views from the trails above the Almaden and Santa Clara valleys. The secluded highland valley of the park provides a quiet episode for exploring the natural surroundings of the surrounding developed areas. Santa Teresa County Park is located at the southern end of Santa Teresa. The park can be accessed from the Alma Mountain Valley or Santa Clara Valley. From the Santa Clara Valley, take the US 101 or 85 motorway to the Bernal Road exit. Drive 1.3 miles west along Bernal Road and cross Santa Teresa Avenue to Santa Teresa. Bernal Road continues through the park's Santa Teresa Golf Club and enters the hills. Located on Bernal Road, Pueblo Day Use Area is set in a small open valley on a hill.
